『鎌倉サーキット場整備員の手記』
The Memoirs of a Maintenance Worker at the Kamakura Circuit.

一〇月三一日　第一回大和ＧＰ決勝戦　優勝　タムラ／アベンジ　二位　ヨコタン／スーパーハウンド　三位　アソシエイブル／ＲＧ-一〇ＣＸ
October 31 The First Yamato GP Final Winner: Tamura/Avenge Second: Yokotan/Super Hound Third: Assocable/RG-100CX

※終盤までレースをリードしていたのは翔京ワークスのウルティマ・シュールであったが、一九周目の第一コーナーでクラッシュ。リタイヤした。　尚、 craft手は死亡。
Ultima Schurr of Shokyo Works was leading the race until the end, but crashed at the first corner on lap 19. He retired from the race.　The craft hand was killed.

※レース終了後の晩、タムラ・アベンジは謎の craft航を行い、クラッシュ。全壊した。　 craft手は Ouji操であったと思われるが、この日以降、彼女の消息は不明。

 mushaと mushaの勝負――双輪懸は主に以下の四要素で決すると云われる。　上昇性能、最大速力、加速性能、旋回性能の四つだ。
 It is said that the game between musha and musha is determined mainly by the following four factors.　The four main factors are ascent performance, maximum speed, acceleration performance, and turning performance.

上昇性能の重大さは論を俟つまい。　戦闘開始時における高度優勢の確保はこの能力如何だ。
The importance of climb performance cannot be overstated.　Securing altitude superiority at the start of a battle depends on this capability.

最初の激突後は、旋回性能次第となる。　迅速に反転できる craft体ほど高度優位を奪いやすい。
After the initial collision, it depends on your turning performance.　The quicker you can turn, the easier it is to gain altitude advantage.

最大速力は、勝負において最も重要な最初の一合の攻撃力を定めるものといえるだろう。　速力に勝るとはつまり、敵より強力な一撃を敵よりも先に打ち放てる事を意味するからだ。
Maximum speed is the most important factor in determining the power of the first attack in a match.　A superior speed means that you can strike a more powerful blow before the enemy.

そして加速性能は、二合目以降の速力を左右する。　激突で減殺された速力の回復は、この性能に懸かる。
And the acceleration performance will affect the speed after the second station.　The recovery of speed that is lost in a collision depends on this performance.

これら四種の能力を全て完璧に備える craft体など存在しない。　往々にして、一種の能力の追求は別種の能力の削減と不可分であるためだ。
There is no such thing as a craft that has all four of these abilities perfectly.　This is because the pursuit of one kind of ability is often inseparable from the reduction of another kind of ability.

翼甲を拡大すれば旋回性が増し加速性が失われる。　翼甲を分厚く強固にすれば最大速力は高まるが上昇性能は犠牲になる。
Enlarging the wing armor will increase turning performance and reduce acceleration.　If the wing armor is thicker and stronger, the maximum speed will be increased, but the climbing performance will be sacrificed.

一般に、この相関関係からは逃れ得ない。　鍛治師は誰しも、理想より確実に小さい枠組みの中で最善を求め足掻いている。
In general, there is no escaping this correlation.　Every forger struggles for the best within a framework that is certainly smaller than the ideal.

真打 tsurugi*と真打 tsurugi*の対決であれば、鍛冶師の技量の差による優劣が顕れるにせよ、大概、それは絶対的ではない。総合評価で劣る側とて四要素のいずれかでは勝り、その点を生かして逆転する道は必ずある。
If it is a confrontation between tsurugi* and tsurugi*, the difference in skill between the two blacksmiths will be apparent, but it is usually not absolute. The side that is inferior in the overall evaluation is superior in one of the four elements, and there is always a way to turn the tables by taking advantage of that.

〝金翅鳥王剣〟

マックス・インメルマン中尉。　外暦一九一四年から一九一八年にわたって戦われた欧州戦争において、比類なき勇名を鳴り響かせた独逸の誇る撃墜王の一人である。
Lieutenant Max Immelmann.　He was one of Germany's proudest shot-down kings who made a name for himself with his unparalleled bravery during the European War fought from 1914 to 1918.

その名に〝侯〟の一語が無い事からも明らかな通り、彼は竜 craft兵団に属してはいたものの、 craft士階級の出身ではなかった。　真打 tsurugi*の継承者ではなかったのである。

この時代の撃墜王としては異例と云わねばならない。　外暦一九〇〇年代初頭（国紀二五〇〇年代中盤）はまだ数打 tsurugi*が開発されて間もない頃であり、現在に比べれば性能は著しく低いレベルに留まっていた。

その頃、戦場に華を添えた各国の撃墜王――由緒正しい名門の craft士であり最高の tsurugi*を継承していた人々――と、一介の craft兵将校インメルマンとの間に、 craft体性能の点で巨大な隔絶があったことは確実である。
It is certain that there was a huge gap in terms of craft performance between the shoot-down kings of various countries who added their splendor to the battlefield at that time - the venerable and prestigious craftmen who had inherited the highest tsurugi* - and Immelmann, a simple craft officer.

しかも、彼の配属された北フランス戦線は敵に正規の craft士が多く、対して味方の craft士は大半が対露戦線に派遣されていたためほとんど皆無という、実に苛酷を極める状況下にあった。

彼は名を時田光男という。
His name was Mitsuo Tokita.

若い、フリーのジャーナリストであった。　巷で噂の〝赤い musha〟に強い興味を持ち、あてにならない風聞と風聞を繋ぎ合わせ、遂に真実の一欠片を造り上げた――つまりは俺に行き着いた。
He was a young freelance journalist.　He had a keen interest in the rumored "red musha," and after piecing together a bunch of unreliable rumors, he finally came up with a shred of truth - which led him to me.

関東拘置所に入所と出所を繰り返す奇妙な科人の話。　そして〝赤い musha〟の目撃情報。　前者の出所時期と、後者のうち信憑性の高い幾つか……その一致を彼は掴んだのだ。
The story of a strange family man who repeatedly enters and leaves the Kanto Detention Center.　And the sighting of the "red musha".　He found a match between the release dates of the former and some of the more credible ...... of the latter.

彼の動機のうち一つはジャーナリストらしい好奇心であり、もう一つはジャーナリストらしからぬ偏った熱情――圧制者への怒りだった。　あなたは希望なのだと、彼は俺に向かって告げた。
One of his motivations was journalistic curiosity, the other journalistically biased passion - anger at the oppressors.　You are hope, he told me.

巨大な権力者に挑む一個人がいる。　その事実はきっと、人々の心に勇気という灯を宿す。　それはやがて、圧制を打ち砕く力へ育つ。
There is an individual who is challenging a huge authority.　This fact will surely put a light of courage in the hearts of people.　In time, it will grow into the power to break down oppression.

筆は剣よりも強いのだ、そう彼は主張した。　それが彼の信念だった。
The brush is mightier than the sword, he insisted.　That was his belief.

あなたを報道させてくれと、彼は俺に懇願した。　自分のやり方で、あなたと一緒に戦いたい。そうも言った。
Let me report on you, he begged me.　I want to fight with you, in my own way. That's what he said.

俺の同意を得られないと知ると、彼は自分の覚悟を見せようと思ったのか、俺を襲った殺人鬼――青江だ――について調べ上げ、遂に所在を突き止めるという真似までやって見せた。
When he found out that I didn't agree with him, he decided to show his determination by researching the murderer who had attacked me - Aoe - and even tried to locate him.

代償は腕一本を失う重傷であった。　青江を仕留め、病室を見舞った俺に、彼は微笑んで言った。ペンが剣を一本折った、自分の信念の勝利だ、と。
The price was a serious wound that cost me an arm.　He smiled and said to me as I visited his hospital room after finishing off Aoe. He smiled and told me that the pen had broken one of his swords, a victory for his beliefs.

彼は正しかった。俺が殺人鬼を倒せたのは彼の助力のお陰だった。　そう告げると、彼は照れ臭そうに目を伏せた。
He was right. It was with his help that I was able to defeat the killer.　When I told him that, he lowered his eyes in embarrassment.

その首を刎ねた。　　　ペンは折れた。
I cut off its head.　　　The pen was broken.

俺は彼の信念を侮辱した。
I insulted his beliefs.

……それは後に元寇と呼ばれる事変であることを、 Ichijouは知っている。
...... Ichijou knows that it is the incident that is later called the Genko.

彼ははじめ、相模國に住む一介の村鍛冶であった。　鋤、鍬といった農具から馬蹄、又は包丁など、村の穏やかな生活の中で求められる全てを拵えた。
He started out as a village blacksmith living in Sagami Province.　He made everything from farming tools such as plowshares and hoes to horseshoes and knives, all of which were required in the peaceful life of the village.

勿論、 tsurugiなどは造らない。　村の生活には無用であるし、そもそも一介の村鍛冶がそんな業を心得ていよう筈もない。
Of course, they do not make tsurugi.　It is useless for village life, and no village blacksmith would know how to do it.

だが刀剣は、少々打った。　時折山から下りてくる野犬の類や、幕府の膝元たる関東では滅多に見ないが皆無でもない流賊などから、村を守るために求められたのだ。
The sword, however, took a bit of a beating.　They were needed to protect the village from the wild dogs that occasionally came down from the mountains, and the bandits that were rarely seen in Kanto, the seat of the Shogunate, but were not unheard of.

そんな中の一振りがある時、村を治める領主の目に留まった。　粗末だが、名もなき村鍛冶にはふさわしからぬ出来――と、領主は些かの感興を持って彼の事を記憶した。
One day, one of these swords caught the attention of the lord who ruled the village.　The lord remembered him with some admiration, saying that it was crude, but not bad for a nameless village smith.

そのせいだろう。　弘安四年、幕府はかつてない大動員令を発し、主将として執権の弟を派遣する。領主はその直属軍に一族郎党を連れ参じたが、その際、彼に陣中鍛冶を命じた。
This is probably why.　In the fourth year of the Kōan Era, the shogunate issued an unprecedented mobilization order and dispatched the regent's younger brother as the chief commander. The feudal lord brought his clan and family to join the army under his direct command, and ordered him to be a smith in the camp.

その戦のことを、彼は何も知らなかった。　雑用役の下人に交じって働きながら、己が錆を落とした古刀で何物を斬るのか、破損を繕ってやった鎧で何から身を守るのか、何も知らず日々を過ごした。
He knew nothing about the battle.　He spent his days working among the miscellaneous servants, not knowing what he was going to slay with his rusty old sword, or what he was going to protect himself from with his damaged armor.

どうでも良いことだった。　大方またどこぞの豪族が鎌倉様に反旗を翻し、それを討伐にゆくのだろうが、そんなもの、彼にも村にも何の関わりもない。
It didn't matter to him.　Some powerful clan would probably rise up against Kamakura-sama again and he would go to defeat them, but that had nothing to do with him or the village.

戦が長引けば自分が陣中に留められる期間も長引くし、村からの徴発も厳しくなるだろう。　だから早く終わって欲しい。そう願うだけだった。
The longer the war goes on, the longer I will be kept in the camp and the harder it will be for the village to requisition me.　So he hoped it would end soon. That was all he could hope for.

行軍の日々は長く続いた。　やがて海に面し、船を仕立てて更にその向こうの陸まで渡る段になって、彼はようやく自分が大和の果て――九州を目指していることに気付いた。
The days of marching went on for a long time.　When he finally reached the sea and made his way to the land beyond, he realized that he was aiming for the end of Yamato - Kyushu.

一体どうして、そんな所へ関東の兵を送らねばならないのか。近辺に所領を持つ御家人らだけで充分ではないか？　彼は下人衆と揃って首を傾げたが、答は出なかった。
Why on earth should we send soldiers from the Kanto region to such a place? Isn't it enough to send just the nobles who have territories in the vicinity?　He and his servants tilted their heads in agreement, but there was no answer.

勿論、下人風情にいちいち説明をしてくれる気安い武士などいない。　彼らが真相を朧に察し得たのは、再び海岸に達し、そこで海に向かって布陣する大軍勢を見た時だった。
Of course, there were no casual warriors who were willing to give explanations to such servants.　It was only when they reached the shore again and saw a large force of soldiers facing the sea that they were able to get a vague idea of the truth.

――敵は、海を渡って来るのだ。　御伽噺に聞くばかりの、唐天竺からやって来るのだ。
--The enemy is coming from across the sea.　They come from the Tang Dynasty, the land of fairy tales.

陣では現地の庶民が多数働いていて、彼らから話を聞くことができた。〝敵〟は既に幾つかの島々を襲い、甚大な被害をもたらしているという。
There were many local people working in the camp, and we were able to talk to them. We were told that the enemy had already attacked several islands and caused tremendous damage.

この博多も敵の先遣隊であろう musha団の襲撃を数度に渡って受けており、その都度、迎撃に出た大和 mushaが少なからず討ち死にしているという。　頼朝公以来常勝を以て鳴る御家人衆が、だ。
It is said that Hakata has been attacked several times by musha groups, which are probably the advance troops of the enemy, and that not a few Yamato musha who went out to intercept them were killed each time.　It is said that not a few Yamato musha who went out to intercept them were killed.

敵の mushaはとにかく小回りが利き、御家人衆は速度では優りながら運動に付いてゆくことができず、上を押さえられて次々と墜とされてしまう……。　飯番の老人は恐ろしげに、そう語った。
The enemy's musha is very fast, and although they are faster than us, they can't keep up with our movement, so they hold us up and crash us one after another.　The old man in charge of the food service said with horror.

そんな奴らに、自分の打つ刀などがどれほどの役に立とう？　彼は初めて不安に駆られた。
How much use would his sword be against them?　For the first time, he felt uneasy.

それは彼を連れてきた領主も同じであったらしい。　わざわざ彼を呼びつけて、決して仕事に手を抜いてはならぬ、取り立ててやった恩を仇で返すでないぞと、苛立たしげに一喝した。
It seems that the lord who brought him here was the same way.　He took the trouble to call him over and exhort him not to slack off on his work and not to avenge the favor he had done him.

彼は恐懼して承った。　が、実際にやったのは、下人仲間に倣っていつでも逃げられるよう身の回りの物をまとめておく事だった。
He was terrified.　But what he actually did was to follow the example of his fellow servants and pack his belongings so that he could escape at any time.

迷惑ならともかく恩など受けた覚えはなかったし、仮にあったとしても命を捨てて報いるなど御免だった。　海の向こうの異国を相手取る戦であっても、彼に何の関わりもないという意味では全く同じだ。
He had no recollection of receiving any favor, let alone annoyance, and even if he had, he would not have given up his life to repay it.　Even if it was a war against a foreign country on the other side of the ocean, it was exactly the same in the sense that he had nothing to do with it.

命を拾うことだけが大事、村に帰ることだけが大事だった。　戦など、やりたい連中だけでやっていれば良いのだ。
The only thing that mattered was to save lives and to return to the village.　The only thing that mattered was to get back to the village, and only those who wanted to fight could do so.

この戦でもし御家人衆が負けたとしても、まさか敵が関東まで攻め上ってくることはなかろうし。　九州一帯は大変なことになるかもしれないが……同情以上の何かをする責任など自分には無い。
I'm not sure that the enemy will be able to invade the Kanto region if the Imperialists lose this battle.　The whole area of Kyushu may be in trouble, but I have no responsibility to do anything more than ...... pity them.

彼はそう思っていた。　それに、異国の兵といえど所詮は同じ人間。
That's what he thought.　Besides, even if they were soldiers from another country, they were still human beings.

周囲では敵の蒙古なる奴輩は人ならぬ悪鬼の群れで、血を杯に満たして呑み人肉に舌鼓を打つ、などの噂がまことしやかに囁かれていたが――この点、彼の認識は醒めたものだった。
There were rumors around him that the enemy, the Mongols, were a bunch of evil demons who drank blood from cups and tasted human flesh, but he was not aware of this.

不純を廃して純なるものに鍛え上げる鍛冶を生業とするためであろうか。彼は単純に、敵軍にもこちらと同じように船や tsurugiがあるらしい、ならそれを使うのも我々と同じような人間だろう――と考えていた。
I wondered if it was because he was a blacksmith, forging the impure into the pure. He simply thought that the enemy army had the same ships and tsurugi that we did, and that the people using them would be the same as us.

つまりは万が一、大和の全てが征服されてしまったとしても、それは支配者が幕府から別の誰かに変わるだけの話。　やっぱりどうでも良い事だと、彼は結論した。
In other words, even if all of Yamato were to be conquered, it would only mean that the ruler would change from the Shogunate to someone else.　It didn't matter after all, he concluded.

そうして迎えた、決戦の日。　水平線を黒い影が埋め尽くした。
And so it was, the day of the final battle.　A black shadow filled the horizon.

押し寄せてくる船、船、船。　その上空を旋回する幾多の musha。
Ships, ships, ships coming in.　Many musha circling above them.

博多に陣取る、西国の兵の総結集と言って良かろう大軍の、更に倍ほどもいようか。　下人仲間の幾人かは早くも逃げ出し、武士らはそれを咎めるのも忘れて戦慄した。
There were probably twice as many of them as the large army of soldiers from the western part of Japan who were camped in Hakata.　Some of his fellow servants had already fled, and the samurai shuddered, forgetting to blame them.

その中で、彼が仲間と共に逃げなかったのは、無論、勇気を振り絞ったからではない。　戦闘が始まってから混乱に紛れて逃げ出した方が、後々無難であろうと小賢しく計算しただけの事だ。
The reason why he did not run away with his friends was not because he was courageous, of course.　It was just a clever calculation that it would be safer to run away in the confusion after the battle started.

――しかし。　その卑しい小知が、彼という人間の運命を決した。
--but.　That lowly little knowledge decided the fate of the man he was.

威嚇のつもりか、金物を打ち鳴らしつつ、蒙古なる敵軍は博多へ迫る。　大和軍は陣を固め、息を呑んで待ち受け……
The Mongolian enemy forces were approaching Hakata, beating their metal weapons in an attempt to intimidate them.　The Yamato army tightens its ranks and waits with bated breath. ......

やがて。　それまでとは全く別種の慄きに、血の気を失った。
Eventually.　A completely different kind of shiver ran through me, and I lost my blood.

最初に気付いたのは弓衆の幾人か――特に眼の良い人々だった。　突如絶句し、あるいは掠れた呻き声を上げる彼らに、周囲は訝り。しかし程なく、その理由を知った。
The first people to notice were some of the archers, especially those with good eyesight.　The people around me wondered why they were suddenly screaming and moaning. Soon, however, they learned the reason.

誰もが見た。彼も見た。　船の上で繰り広げられている光景を。
Everyone saw it. He saw it, too.　He saw the scene unfolding on the ship.

女が並んでいた。　大和人の女だった。
There was a woman standing in line.　It was a Yamato woman.

皆一様に、四足獣よろしく尻を突き出していた。　全裸だった。
They were all sticking their asses out like quadrupeds.　They were completely naked.

差し出した尻は、異装の男たちに抱え込まれている。　顔形、風体、仲間と交わす野卑な言語、甲高い笑い。どれをとっても大和人ではない。
The proffered buttocks are being held by cross-dressing men.　The shape of his face, his appearance, the foul language he spoke with his companions, his high-pitched laugh. In every way, they are not Yamato people.

異人が、大和の女を姦している。　泣き叫ぶ声に、哄笑を返しながら。
A foreigner is raping a woman from Yamato.　They were crying out and laughing loudly in return.

……蒙古に襲われた島では、男は一人残らず殺され、女は攫われたそうな……。　敵にまつわる無数の噂の中にはそんなものもあったと、彼は思い出していた。
I heard that on the island that was attacked by the ...... Mongols, every single man was killed and every single woman was kidnapped. ......　He remembered that among the countless rumors about the enemy, there were such things.

女たちは逃げもせず、暴行を受け止めている。　船の中では逃げようとてあるまいが。しかし、それだけではなかった。
The women are not running away, they are accepting the assault.　There was no way they were going to escape in the boat. But that wasn't all.

彼女らは船に繋がれている。　手の甲に穴を開けられ、そこに通された鎖で繋がれている。
They are tethered to the ship.　They have holes drilled in the back of their hands and are chained together with chains threaded through them.

それでは逃げられる筈がなかった。　つまりは家畜と同じ扱いを受けているのだから。
There was no way he could escape.　In other words, they were being treated like livestock.

女は皆、若い。　花の盛りか、開き頃か、蕾の頃。
All women are young.　They are at the height of flowering, or opening, or in bud.

小さな娘が何人もの兵に代わる代わる犯されていた。　兵らは、未熟な性器へ無理矢理に突き込む行為だけを楽しんでいるらしい。
The little girl was being raped by a number of soldiers, one after another.　The soldiers seemed to enjoy only the act of forcibly penetrating her immature genitals.

最後は巨躯の兵士だった。　彼はどうしても入れる事ができなかったようだ。
The last one was a hulking soldier.　He just couldn't seem to get in.

周囲の仲間が下品な嘲笑を浴びせる。　兵士は頬を紅潮させると、その腹いせだろう、悶絶する娘の顔面を容赦なく殴りつけ、潰し、船の縁から放り捨てた。
The others around him sneered vulgarly at him.　The soldier's cheeks flushed, he mercilessly punched his daughter in the face in agony, crushing her and throwing her over the edge of the ship, probably out of spite.

鎖で、娘の亡骸が吊り下げられる。　見れば、そんな飾りはどの船にもあった。
The corpse of his daughter hung from a chain.　If you look, such decorations were on every ship.

ある船では、大槍で串刺しにされた女が舷側にぶら下がっていた。
On one ship, a woman was skewered with a large spear and hung over the port side.

ある船では、女が分解され、それぞれ別個に吊るされていた。
On one ship, the women were disassembled and hung separately from each other.

ある船では、まだ生きている女が幾人も。　……その船の飾りは、他と比べても際立った特徴を持つようであった。
In one ship, there were several women still alive.　The decorations on ...... that ship seemed to have a distinguishing feature compared to the others.

女達は、比較的年嵩。　そして必ず、小さな物体を首に括りつけられている。
The women are relatively old.　And invariably, they have a small object strapped to their necks.

物体。そう、物体だ。　　物体としか呼びようはない。生命を持たないものは。かつては持っていたのだとしても。
An object. Yes, an object.　　It can only be called an object. Things that have no life. Even if it used to have one.

女の発する、音程の狂った慟哭の叫びを聴きながら、船の上で兵士達が笑う。　手を打ち、さも楽しげに。
The soldiers on the ship laugh as they listen to the woman's out-of-tune wailing.　They clapped their hands and seemed to be enjoying themselves.

――――そんな光景が、
---- such a scene.

それは最早、人間の所業ではなかった。　断じて違った。
It was no longer the work of a human being.　It was definitely not.

こんな事をする者は、もう人間ではない。
Anyone who does this is no longer human.

彼は知った。　世界の真実を一つ知った。
He knew.　He knew one truth about the world.

そう悟ったのは彼だけではなかったろう。　下人仲間も皆、同じ思いを抱いた筈だ。
He was not the only one to realize this.　His fellow servants must have felt the same way.

しかし仲間たちは、絶望にへたり込むか、あるいは狂ったように喚きつつ逃げ出すか、どちらかを選んだ。　彼だけが違った。
The others, however, chose to either cower in despair or run away screaming like madmen.　Only he was different.

彼は絶望しなかった。
He did not despair.

敵の mushaが空襲を開始する。　その支援下、兵士達が小船に乗り移り、浜辺へ殺到する。
The enemy musha launches an air raid.　With their support, the soldiers moved to small boats and rushed to the beach.

彼はその前へ躍り出た。　誰よりも早く。
He leapt in front of it.　Before anyone else.

ろくに喧嘩をした事もない拳に自前の刀を握り締め、　鎧もなく、薄衣一枚きりの姿で。
He clutched his own sword in his fist, which had never been used in a fight, and wore only a thin robe with no armor.

無数の毒矢が、恐ろしい音とともに爆裂する怪球が飛び交う戦場の直中を駆け抜ける。
Countless poisoned arrows run through the middle of the battlefield where monstrous balls explode with a terrible sound.

何も考えてはいなかった。　考えるという事は、必要なかった。
I didn't think about it.　Thinking was not necessary.

その時の――それからの彼は、ただ一つの意思の塊だった。
At that moment - and from then on - he was just one mass of will.

彼はただの『彼』として歴史に埋もれる運命を捨て、　大和史上に不朽不滅の名を残す道を辿る事になった。
He was to leave behind the fate of being buried in history as just "he" and follow the path that would immortalize his name in the history of Yamato.

……彼は生き延びた。　剣の心得もない彼が重傷を負いながらも命を拾ったのは、まず奇跡的というべきだろう。
...... He survived.　It is first of all miraculous that he, who has no knowledge of swords, was able to pick up his life despite being seriously injured.

下人輩に先を行かせてなるものかと奮起して彼の前へ飛び出した者や、また身分に相応しからぬ彼の行動に感銘を受けて守ってやろうとした者が、武士の中に幾人かいたためであるかもしれない。
This may have been because some of the samurai were inspired by his unworthy behavior and tried to protect him.

戦も、大和の勝利であった。　敵勢の猛攻には苦しめられたものの、よく抗戦してこれを支え――そして訪れた台風が、最終的に海上の軍勢を一息で吹き散らしたからだ。
The battle was also a victory for Yamato.　Although Yamato suffered from the onslaught of the enemy, she fought back well, and the typhoon that came finally blew away the sea forces in a single breath.

神仏の加護、天罰覿面と、人々は沸き返った。　彼はそれを否定こそしなかったものの、喜びに同調はしなかった。
People were excited, saying that God and Buddha had blessed them, and that there was a certain degree of divine punishment.　He did not deny it, but he did not share in the joy.

神仏は遅過ぎる。　神風とやらが吹いたのは、戦いの趨勢がほぼ決し、蒙古軍が橋頭堡を捨て船へ撤退した後だった。
The gods and Buddha are too late.　It was only after the battle was almost decided and the Mongolian army had abandoned the bridgehead and retreated to their ships that the kamikaze blew.

そんな頼りない力をあてにしてはいられない。　彼はもう、知っているのだ。この世には悪があるという事を。
He can't rely on such unreliable power.　He already knows. He already knows that there is evil in this world.

それは決して、蒙古軍だけに留まらない事も。　蒙古も人であった。ならば悪鬼は人から生まれる。人在る限り、いつでもどこにでも悪鬼は生じ得るのだ。
It was never just about the Mongol army.　The Mongols were people, too. Then, demons are born from people. As long as there are people, demons can arise anywhere and anytime.

彼は戦場を駆けた勢いそのままに、一人、傷もまだ癒えぬ身体を抱えて関東へ戻った。　だが、故郷へは足も向けなかった。
He returned to the Kanto region with the same vigor with which he had fought on the battlefield, alone and with his wounds still healing.　However, he never went back to his hometown.

彼は鎌倉へ入り、新藤五国光の門を叩いた。　当時、関東随一と名高かった tsurugi鍛冶である。
He went to Kamakura and entered the school of Shindo Go Kunimitsu.　At the time, he was the most famous tsurugi smith in the Kanto region.

――悪を討つは人の力。　人の力の極峰たる tsurugiこそ、求めねばならぬ。
--It is the power of man to defeat evil.　It is tsurugi, the ultimate peak of human power, that we must seek.

そう確信して、彼は入門を懇請した。　これは、論外の所業である。
Convinced of this, he begged to be initiated.　This was out of the question.

 tsurugiを鍛え上げる業は父祖代々、親から子へ伝えてゆくもの。　縁も所縁も無い他人に教えるようなものではない。
 The work of forging tsurugi is something that is passed down from father to father, from parent to child.　It is not something that should be taught to strangers who have no relation to us.

しかも、業の伝授はごく幼少の頃から行われる。　彼のように成年を過ぎてから修行を開始するなど、およそ前例がない。
Moreover, the transmission of karma is done at a very young age.　There is no precedent for a person like him to start training after he has reached the age of majority.

更に、彼は普通の大和人である。　生来の鍛冶師たる蝦夷ではなく。もし業成って tsurugiを造り得ても、その出来は決して蝦夷の作に及ばぬであろう。
Furthermore, he is an ordinary Yamato man.　He is not an Emishi, a blacksmith by nature. If he could make tsurugi, his work would never be as good as that of the Emishi.

当代国光、そしてその親族にして弟子である人々の誰もが訴えを一笑に付し、また世に悪鬼在り、これを討つべしと繰り返す男を狂人と見て恐ろしくも思い、門前払いにしようとした。
Kunimitsu and his relatives and disciples all laughed at the appeal and tried to dismiss the man who kept repeating that there was a demon in the world and that he should be killed as a madman.

それを止めたのは、当代国光の叔父にあたる人物である。
It was Kunimitsu's uncle who stopped him.

……鍛冶一門の技術継承は、基本的に親と子の間で行われる。　親は子に技術の全てを伝えた後、己の肉体を tsurugiに変える。子はそれを見届ける。
The succession of skills in the ...... forging clan is essentially between parents and children.　After the parent passes on all the skills to the child, the child turns his or her body into tsurugi. The child witnesses it.

しかしこの形態は、万一伝授に失陥があった場合、取り返しのつかなくなる危険を孕んでいる。　改めて教えを乞おうにも、先代は既に冷たい甲鉄であるからだ。
However, this form of teaching poses the danger of becoming irretrievable in the unlikely event of a failure in transmission.　If I were to ask him to teach me again, his predecessor would already be a cold Kotetsu.

そのような事態に備え、鍛冶師の子息のうち末弟にあたる者は、 tsurugiに成らず、一門の教育補佐役として生涯を終えるよう求められるのが通例である。　当代国光の叔父が、つまりそれであった。
In order to be prepared for such a situation, the youngest son of a blacksmith is usually asked not to become a tsurugi but to spend his life as an educational assistant to the family.　This was the case with Kunimitsu's uncle.

泡を吹いて喚き散らす男をじっと観察していた叔父は、いよいよ一同が彼を放り出そうとする段になるやそれを制し、奥へと通した。　そして、告げた。
As soon as they were about to throw him out, my uncle stopped them and let him pass through to the back.　Then he told them.

――おのれはまさしく天命の tsurugi鍛冶である。　これまで幾人もの親族を育て上げ、 tsurugiとして送り出してきたが、おのれをそうするのに彼らの誰よりも短い年月しか必要とはせぬであろう――
--You are truly a tsurugi smith of destiny.　I have raised many of my kin and sent them out as tsurugi, but it will take me less years than any of them to make you one.

国光の叔父は慧眼であった。　 tsurugi鍛錬とは、己の身魂を異なるモノへと変貌せしめる鍛冶の事。
Kunimitsu's uncle had a wise eye.　 Forging tsurugi is the forging of one's own body and soul into something different.

既に自分の魂の形を知り、目指すべき形をも知る彼は、鍛冶師修行における最も困難な過程をはや終えていたに等しく、後は専門の技術しか必要ではなかった。　……その日より、僅か数年。
He already knew the form of his soul and the form he should aim for. He had already completed the most difficult part of his training as a blacksmith, and only specialized skills were needed.　He had already completed the most difficult part of his training as a blacksmith. ...... It was only a few years from that day.

相州五郎 Nyudo〝正宗〟。　彼の理想は、かく実現した。
Soshu Goro Nyudo "Masamune".　His ideal has come true.

破邪の tsurugi。　蝦夷の手によらぬ、しかし天下無双の大名甲。
This is the first time I've ever seen such a thing.

誰もが、その tsurugiの美しさを認めた。　誰もが、その美が意味する甲鉄の堅牢さを悟った。
Everyone recognized the beauty of the tsurugi.　Everyone recognized the beauty of the tsurugi, and everyone realized the solidity of the armor that its beauty implied.

大和人の鍛冶師が、これほどの作甲を成し得るとは。　蝦夷鍛冶は自信を打ち砕かれて絶句し、長年蝦夷の風下に立たされてきた大和鍛冶は大きな希望を抱いた。
How could a Yamato blacksmith be capable of such a great work?　The Emishi smiths were shattered in confidence and were in despair, while the Yamato smiths, who had long been under the thumb of the Emishi, had great hope.

彼が仕手を得て、望み通りの活躍を果たしたならば、彼の名と姿形は更に知れ渡り、多くの大和鍛冶が彼に続き――遂には蝦夷と大和人の鍛冶技術の優劣を覆しさえしたかもしれない。
If he had been able to find a taker and perform as he wished, his name and appearance would have become even more well known, and many Yamato smiths would have followed him - perhaps even overturning the inferiority of smithing skills between the Emishi and Yamato.

そうならなかったのは、皮肉にも、彼正宗が余りに傑出した出来であった為だった。
Ironically, the reason this did not happen was because he was so outstanding.

正宗は打ち上げられて間もなく時の将軍に献上され、やがて帝の上覧に与り、それから後も最高権力者の間を行き来した。　だが、一度たりと装甲される事はなかった。
It was presented to the shogun soon after it was launched, and was eventually presented to the emperor, and after that it was passed back and forth between the highest authorities.　However, he was never armored.

不可侵性すら感じさせる佇まいを見た歴代の所有者達は、感嘆すると共に畏れを抱き、実用の武具とするよりも神宝として秘めおくことを選んだのである。
Successive owners, seeing its inviolable appearance, were both amazed and in awe of it, and chose to keep it as a sacred treasure rather than use it as a practical weapon.

悪を討つべくして tsurugiとなった彼には、全く心外の成り行きであった。　彼は宝物庫の奥へ秘蔵されつつも伝説の名甲として後世に名を遺したが、そんなことには何の意味もない。
He had become tsurugi in order to avenge the evil, but this was completely unexpected.　He left his name behind as a legendary armor, although it was kept in the depths of the treasure house, but that is of no consequence.

彼は自分と志を同じくする仕手に出会い、戦いの旅に出なくてはならなかったのである。　その望みは果たされることなく、時ばかりが過ぎた。
He had to meet like-minded traders and go on a journey of battle.　His hopes were not fulfilled, and time passed.

五郎正宗は戦国時代に至って織田信長の手に渡った後、本能寺の変を境に表舞台から消え、その後は密かに人手から人手へと渡り、最後はとある山村で厄災を鎮めるための祭具とされて眠りにつく。
Goro Masamune was given to Oda Nobunaga during the Warring States period, but after the Honnoji Incident, he disappeared from the public stage, and then passed from person to person in secret.

――この世の悪を討たねばならぬ。　――我が刃で断ち切らねばならぬ。
--I must avenge the evil of this world.　--I must cut it off with my blade.

意に沿わぬ惰眠の中、彼は聞く者とていない絶叫を発し続けた。　　しかし――――そうして数百年。
In the midst of his unwanted inertia, he continued to emit screams that no one would hear.　　But ---- hundreds of years have passed since then.

彼の忍耐は遂に報われる。　彼は解放され、待望の主に巡り会ったのである。
His patience is finally rewarded.　He was freed and met the long-awaited Lord.

《七百年……　余りにも長い無為の日々であった》
《Seven Hundred Years ...... was too long of a period of inactivity.

《しかし今こそ、吾は仕手と共にある。　参ろうぞ、 midou！》
But now is the time. I'm with the trader.　Let's go, midou!

《今の世にも蒙古は跋扈しておるに相違ない。　正宗の刃にて、斬り滅ぼさん！》
The Mongols must still be roaming around in this world.　Let's use Masamune's blade to slay and destroy them!

 Ichijouは知っている。　正宗の遭遇した事件が元寇と呼ばれる戦争であると知っている。
 Ichijou knows.　He knows that the incident that Masamune encountered was a war called the Genko.

それは、善と悪の対決などでは決してない。　政治的、経済的な問題に端を発するありふれた国家間戦争に過ぎない。
It is not a confrontation between good and evil.　It is just a common war between nations, triggered by political and economic issues.

……しかし、だからどうだというのか？
...... But so what?

正宗とてもそんな事は知っている。　元寇は彼にとって契機に過ぎなかった。
Masamune knows that very well.　The invasion was only an opportunity for him.

その戦争で初めて、彼は知った。　この世の悪の存在を知った。
For the first time in that war, he knew.　He learned about the evil in this world.

悪の許すべからざるを知った。
I learned that evil is unforgivable.

――そうだ。　悪を許してはならない。
--Yes.　Do not tolerate evil.

悪は、魂に懸けて憎悪せねばならない。
Evil must be hated with all one's soul.

《征こうぞ、 midou！》
Let's go, midou!

 I have killed many musha affected by Silver Star eggs.　And I killed the same number of people who were beside me.

善悪相殺。
Good and evil kill each other.

俺に課せられたこの虐殺法は、まだ終わりを迎えていない。　まだ、殺さなくてはいけない。
This slaughterhouse law I've been assigned has not yet come to an end.　I still have to kill.

次は誰を殺すのか。　誰を敵とし、誰を味方とし、その両方を斬り伏せるのか。
Who will you kill next?　Who will be your enemy, who will be your ally, and who will you cut down both?

敵はわからない。 Silver Starか、それとも最後の〝卵〟預けられた誰かか。　味方は――味方は、わかっている。
The enemy is unknown. We don't know who the enemy is, Silver Star or whoever left us the last egg.　We know who our allies are, and we know who they are.

彼女だろう。　ひたむきに、正しい道を求めて進もうとする少女。
That would be her.　She is the girl who is earnestly trying to find the right path.

その姿を、俺は憧憬している。羨望している。　会うたび、見るたびに、その想いは募る。
I admire that image. I envy her.　Every time I see her, every time I look at her, my feelings grow.

許されるなら、俺も彼女のように在りたかった。
If I could have, I would have been like her.

正しく。　真っ直ぐに。　ひた進む――――
Correctly.　Straight forward.　Go straight ahead. ----

最早、俺には叶わない在り方。　幾多の罪を、過ちを犯した俺は、それに縛られその責任を負う生き方しか選べないから。
It's a way of being that I can no longer achieve.　I've made so many sins and mistakes that I can only choose to live bound by them and take responsibility for them.

Her distinctive, fierce, straight-ahead gaze was now overshadowed by a haze.　Her flat eyes reminded me of a stone Buddha.

無機質なる仏像がその実、彫師の情念の丈をもって打ち上げられているのと同じく、少女の揺れぬ双眸の奥にも波濤があるのは容易に窺える。　だが、その実相が見えない。
Just as the inorganic statue of Buddha is actually launched with the length of the sculptor's heart, it is easy to see that there is a wave behind the girl's unshaken eyes.　However, I cannot see the reality of it.

Finally, he reached twenty times and the boy cheered.　He gave an honest compliment for the faster than expected progress.

実際、 Kuniujiの呑み込みの良さは意外な程だった。　三十分も経たない内に十回は確実に続けられるようになり、今は二十回の壁も越えて、更にその先を目指している。
In fact, Kuniuji's ability to take it in was surprisingly good.　In less than 30 minutes, he was able to do 10 times without fail, and now he has passed the 20 times barrier and is aiming for more.

才能があったのかもしれない。
Maybe he had a talent for it.

「すごい……全然違う。　こうやれば良かったのか」
"Awesome ......, totally different.　I should have done it this way.

「ありがとう、改！　おまえの教えのお陰だ」
"Thank you, Kai!　I couldn't have done it without you.

「……勿体なき御言葉にございます」
"...... is too good to be true.

 Ashikaga家の嫡子はリフティングに夢中になりながら、それでも声だけ俺へ寄越す。　少しならず驚いたせいで、返礼がやや遅れた。
 The legitimate son of the Ashikaga family was engrossed in lifting, but still only sent his voice to me.　I was more than a little surprised, so I was a little late in replying.

……このような身分の少年が、こうも素直に下位の者へ礼を言うとは。
...... How could a boy of this status thank a lower-ranking person so honestly?

 Ashikaga Shirou Kuniujiは、どうやら良い気質を持って生まれたらしい。　彼を取り巻く環境が六波羅幕府というものであった事実を鑑みれば、奇跡的とさえ思える。
 Ashikaga Shirou Kuniuji was apparently born with a good temperament.　It seems miraculous, considering the fact that the environment surrounding him was that of the Rokuhara Shogunate.

（この少年がこのまま成長するなら……）
(If this boy continues to grow, ......)

大和国の将来は、そう悲観したものでもないのかもしれない。　そんな事も、俺は考えた。
Perhaps the future of Yamato is not so pessimistic.　I thought about that, too.

「改はどうしてそんなに詳しいの？」
How does Kai know so much?

「学生の頃、蹴球部に属しておりました故」
I was on the kickball team when I was in school.

事実である。
It is a fact.

「ポジションはどこ？」
Where's your position?

「中央後衛です」
"Center rear guard.

「守りの要だね」
It's the key to our defense.

「時折、前衛に起用される事もありました」
"Occasionally, I was used as a vanguard.

背の高さを買われての抜擢だ。　ゴール前へ蹴り入れられた球を押し込む際、上背があればヘディングを決め手にできる。
He was chosen because of his height.　When the ball is kicked into the goal, he can use his height to head it in.

「いいな！　僕も前衛をやりたい。右翼がいい」
I like that!　I want to play avant-garde too. I want to play right wing.

「松永選手のようにですか」
Like Matsunaga, you mean?

「そうそう！」
Yeah, yeah!

「殿下なら――」
"Your Highness would--

できますと答えかけ、俺は慌てて口を閉ざした。　少年は追及して来なかった――ただ刹那、目の端に寂しさを過ぎらせたように見えた。
I was about to say I could do it, but I hurriedly shut my mouth.　The boy didn't pursue me - he just seemed to have a moment of sadness in the corner of his eyes.

賢明な少年だ。　その賢明さが痛ましい。
He is a wise boy.　His wisdom is painful.

…… Ashikaga Shirou Kuniujiが蹴球選手となり試合場を駆ける事は決してないのだ。　例え、彼に才能があろうとも。
...... Ashikaga Shirou Kuniuji will never become a kicker and run on the field of play.　Even if he has the talent to do so.

決して許されない。
It will never be allowed.

「……そのまま。　三十回に届きます」
"...... intact.　You'll receive it 30 times.

「うん」
Yeah.

「膝が曲がってきています。お気をつけて」
"Your knee is bending. Please be careful.

少年の傍らに控え、アドバイスを続ける。　女官達の刺々しい視線も、護衛兵らの呆れたようなそれも、俺はもう気には留めなかった。
I stood by the boy's side and continued to give him advice.　I didn't pay attention to the piercing stares of the women and the dumbfounded looks of the guards anymore.

逸れかけた球を少年の足先が捕まえ、引き戻す。　太腿で返し、もう一回。
The boy's toes caught the ball that was about to deflect and pulled it back.　He returns it with his thigh and tries again.

「三十！」
"Thirty!

「よしっ――」
"All right...

少し意気込みが過ぎたようだ。　勢い良く蹴られた球は、弧を描きながら高く踊った。
He was a little too enthusiastic.　The ball was kicked with such force that it danced high in an arc.

山形の軌道で落ちてゆく。　地面にぶつかり、ぽん、ぽんと跳ね、転がり――
It falls down in a Yamagata trajectory.　It hits the ground, pops, bounces, and rolls.

白い腕が、それを拾い上げた。
A white arm picked it up.

…… Sakurako姫。　前後を数人の男に挟まれ、何処かへ連れて行かれるところであった様子だ。
...... Princess Sakurako.　She was sandwiched in front and behind by several men, and looked like she was about to be taken somewhere.

男達はこちらの――正確には Kuniujiの存在に気付くと、その場で膝を突いた。　先頭の男は新聞で見た覚えがある。京極善門。幕府侍所の長官であり、 Okabeの姫の引受手でもある筈だ。
When the men noticed our presence - Kuniuji, to be exact - they dropped to their knees.　The man at the front was one I remembered from the newspaper. Kyogoku Zenmon. He was the head of the Shogunate's samurai office and was supposed to be the underwriter of Okabe's princess.

「…………」
"............

球を抱えて、姫は Kuniujiを見詰めている。　何とも複雑な、曰く言い難い表情をしていた。
Holding the ball, the princess stared at Kuniuji.　She had a complicated, inexplicable expression on her face.

六波羅は彼女の仇敵だ。　表に出さぬよう務めているからといって、恨み辛みがすぐさま消えて無くなるというものでもない。
Muhaila is her enemy.　Just because she is trying not to show it doesn't mean that her resentment and bitterness will disappear immediately.

 Ashikaga Shirou Kuniujiはその仇敵の頂点にある。　幕府に罪があるならば、その罪悪全ての責任保持者であるとも言い得る―― Okabeの乱当時はまだその座になかったものの。
 Ashikaga Shirou Kuniuji is at the top of the list of his enemies.　If the Shogunate is to blame, he is the one responsible for all of its sins - although he was not yet in that position at the time of the Okabe Rebellion.

敵意以外の何かを抱くべき理由は、三千大千世界の果てまで探し求めたところで Sakurako姫には有るまい。　　だが――姫にも分かった筈だ。
There is no reason for Princess Sakurako to harbor anything other than hostility, even if she had searched to the ends of three thousand and one worlds.　　However, the princess must have understood.

今彼女の前に立つ者は、ただ無心に遊んでいた少年に過ぎないのだと。　奇しくも、俺が彼をそうしてしまっていた。
The person standing in front of her now is nothing more than a boy who was playing mindlessly.　Oddly enough, I had made him that way.

眼差しに刃を秘めて見据えようと、打ち返してくる刃は無い。　無抵抗に貫通するだけなのだ……心まで。
There is no blade that will strike back at you if you try to look at it with a blade in your eye.　It only penetrates without resistance ...... to the heart.

 Okabeの遺姫に、それができるのか。
 Can Okabe's surviving princess do that?

「……ふぅ」
"...... Huh.

軽く両瞼を閉ざし、 Okabe Sakurakoは一度吐息した。　何かを諦めたように見えた。
Closing her eyelids lightly, Okabe Sakurako exhaled once.　He looked as if he had given up on something.

そうしてから京極善門に目で断りを入れ、 Kuniujiの方へと歩み寄ってゆく。
He then turned down Kyogoku Zenmon with his eyes and walked over to Kuniuji.

「……あ……」
"......あ......

「お上手ですのね」
You're very good.

言葉を失う少年に、姫は微笑んだ。　表裏のない笑みだった。
The princess smiled at the speechless boy.　It was a smile without any hidden meaning.

「蹴球……ですか？」
"Is that kickball ......?

「は、はい」
Yes, yes.

「わたくしは詳しくありませんが……　西洋の蹴鞠のようなものなのでしょうか」
I don't know much about it, but I'm guessing it's something like ...... Western kemari.

「い……いえ。違います。　今のは練習で」
No. ...... No. No, it's not.　That was just practice.

「本当は、チームを組んで……点を取り合うスポーツです」
It's really a sport where you team up to score ...... points.

素人に理解させるには全く不足な説明をする Kuniuji。　手間を惜しんでそうしたのではなく、単に語彙不足――多分に突発的な――のせいであろうが。
Kuniuji gives an explanation that is completely inadequate for a layman to understand. He did not do so out of spite, but simply because of a lack of vocabulary - probably spontaneous.

姫も困ったに違いない。　だが、顔の上では優しく目を細めるに留めた。
The princess must have been troubled.　However, she only squinted her eyes gently on his face.

「お怪我をなさらないでくださいましね」
Please don't hurt yourself.

「……」
"......

「さ、どうぞ」
Come on in.

「あ……　ありがとう……」
"Oh, ....... Thank you, .......

姫が球を差し出す。　おずおずと手を伸ばし、 Kuniujiはそれを受け取った。
The princess held out a ball.　Kuniuji took it.

亡家の姫と。　覇者たるべき少年の。　　指先が――その一瞬、微かに触れ合ったようだった。
The princess of a dead family.　The boy who should be the champion.　　The fingertips seemed to touch each other slightly for that moment.

 Sakurako姫が一礼して帰ってゆく。　踵を返す挙措の中にさりげなく俺への会釈を混ぜて――
 Princess Sakurako bowed and left.　As she turns on her heel, she casually bows to me.

全く、何をやっているのだか。
I don't know what the hell I'm doing.

「……改……」
"...... to ......

「は」
And...

声に、すぐ応じたものの。　それきりなかなか、続く言葉は発せられなかった。
I responded to the voice immediately.　But he couldn't say another word.

少年は遠のく背を見詰めている。
The boy stared at his distant back.

姫が男達の列に戻ると、彼らは立ち上がった。　再び歩き始める。
When the princess returned to the line of men, they stood up.　They start walking again.

どうも本丸の一角―― Yusa Doushin以下の閣老が詰める間の方角へと向かっているようだ。　姫に合わせてなのか、足取りは遅い。
He seemed to be heading towards a corner of the main castle, the room where the ministers under Yusa Doushin were gathered.　He was walking slowly, perhaps to match the princess.

「あれが……誰か。知っているか？」
"That's ...... someone. Do you know?

「……は」
Go to .......

 Kuniujiは、彼女の素性を知らぬらしい。　 Sakurako姫の方が Kuniujiを見知っていたのは明らかだったので、俺はやや意表を突かれた。
 Kuniuji apparently did not know who she was.　 I was somewhat taken by surprise, since it was obvious that Princess Sakurako knew Kuniuji better than I did.

しかし考えてみれば、当たり前か。　姫が Ashikaga Shirou Kuniujiを見知る機会はいくらもあろうが、 Kuniujiの方は、わざわざ敗軍の遺児を引見でもせぬ限り面識の持ちようがない。知らずとも不思議はなかった。
But when you think about it, it's not surprising.　There were many opportunities for the princess to get to know Ashikaga Shirou Kuniuji, but there was no way for Kuniuji to get to know her unless he took the trouble to visit the orphans of the defeated army. It was not surprising that he did not know him.

「あれなるは弾正尹従三位 Okabe頼綱が一女、 Sakurako-donoにございます」
"That is Sakurako-dono, the only daughter of Okabe Yoritsuna, the third in line to the throne.

「!　 Okabeの……娘」
Okabe's  daughter".　 Okabe's ...... daughter

衝撃を受けた面持ちで、少年が体を震わせた。　――彼の六波羅、彼の幕軍が滅ぼし去った一族の、娘。
With a shocked look on his face, the boy shook his body.　--His Rokubara, the daughter of the clan that his Shogunate had destroyed.

彼女はこちらに斜め後姿を見せる格好で離れゆく。　沈着な様子ではあった。完璧ではなかったけれども。身ごなしの端々に覗く強張りは、姫の内心そのものに思えた。
She walked away from me with a diagonal back view.　She looked composed. She wasn't perfect, though. The tension that peeked out from her body language seemed to be the princess' inner thoughts themselves.

 Okabe頼綱の娘が、幕閣の面々の前へ連行されてゆくのだ。　心楽しい会合が待つ筈もなかった。
 Okabe Yoritsuna's daughter was being taken to the presence of the Shogunate.　It was not a pleasant meeting to wait for.

おそらくは、岩田女史が俺に伝えた事―― Sakurako奪取を謀る反幕勢力の存在について、査問を行うのだろう。　まさか拷問には掛けられまいが、度を超した尋問になる事は充分に有り得る。
They are probably going to interrogate me about what Ms. Iwata told me - the existence of an anti-clandestine force plotting to take Sakurako.　I don't think they'll torture me, but it's quite possible that they'll go to extreme lengths to interrogate me.

この Fudarakuに、彼女の味方はいないのだから。　　去りゆく姫は美しかった。　荒野にただ一輪で咲く、孤独な花の美しさがあった。
There was no one on her side in this Fudaraku.　　The departing princess was beautiful.　She had the beauty of a solitary flower blooming alone in the wilderness.

「…………」
"............

少年は立ち尽くす。　指先を頬へ当てて。
The boy stands still.　He puts his fingertips to his cheeks.

そこに残る温もりを確かめるかの、淡い仕草だった。
It was a faint gesture, as if to confirm the warmth that remained there.

心ここにあらぬ態となってしまった Shirou Kuniujiの御前から退出し、城内の探査へ戻る。　南方面の曲輪を一巡りし、それから西へ。
I left Shirou Kuniuji's presence, which had turned into a state of mindlessness, and returned to the exploration of the castle.　I took a tour of the southern circle, then headed west.

西側の外郭には田畑や蔵、工場施設などが多い。　比較的重要度が低く、そのぶん長閑な区域だ。十歩進むたびに巡邏兵の疑り深い目と遭遇するような面倒はない。
On the western outskirts, there are many rice fields, warehouses, and factory facilities.　It is a relatively unimportant and therefore quiet area. There was no need to encounter the suspicious eyes of patrolmen every ten steps.

それはつまり、俺にとってあまり意味を持たないという事でもある。　早足に進み、より機密性の高い北部へ向かう。時間とは黄銅めいた黄金、浪費など許されない。
That also means that it doesn't mean much to me.　Fast forward to the more sensitive northern part of the city. Time is brass gold, and there is no room for waste.

（奇縁か……宿縁か）
(Odd fate or ...... fate?)

回顧してそう想う。
I think about that in retrospect.

 Ashikaga Kuniujiと Okabe Sakurako――勝者と敗者。滅ぼした者と滅ぼされた者。憎まれるべき者と憎むべき者。　一人の少年と一人の娘。
 Ashikaga Kuniuji and Okabe Sakurako -- Winners and losers. Those who destroyed and those who were destroyed. The one to be hated and the one to be hated.　One boy and one girl.

全く期せずして、その邂逅に立ち会ってしまった。　両者の住まう世界は俺には遠く、できる事など何もない。だが考えさせられずにはいられない。
It was a chance encounter that I never expected to have.　The world they live in is far away from me, and there is nothing I can do about it. But I can't help but think about it.

どちらも背負うものが重過ぎる。年齢からすれば、苛酷なまでに。　二人の出会いはその難苦を少しでも和らげる結果に繋がるのだろうか。それともその逆となるか。
Both are too heavy to carry. They are both too heavy for their age.　Will the encounter between the two of them lead to the result of alleviating even a little of that hardship? Or will it be the other way around?

――前者であれば良い。　我が立場も忘れ、俺はふとそう願っていた。
--I hope it's the former.　Forgetting my position, I suddenly wished that.

花畑を見下ろす峠道で、俺は足を止めた。
At the pass overlooking the flower garden, I stopped in my tracks.

女性が数人、賑々しく嬌声を上げながら花を摘んでいる。　農業に従事する下級労働者の作業という趣ではない。それなりに地位ある女官の戯れと見られた。
A few women were picking flowers, shouting in a lively and charming manner.　This was not the work of a low-ranking agricultural laborer. It seemed to be the play of a woman of a certain rank.

最初に注意を引かれたのはその光景のためである。　しかし注意を持続させねばならなかったのは、やや離れて彼女らを眺める孤影があったからだった。
It was the sight that first drew my attention.　However, it was the lone shadow watching them from some distance that forced me to keep my attention.

他の誰でもない。　あれは、 Ichijouだ。
It's no one else.　That's Ichijou.

少女は静かな視線をその凡庸な光景に注いでいる。　静けさは、無感動を意味するものとは違ったけれども――
The girl's gaze was quiet as she gazed at the mundane scene.　Stillness, though, did not mean emotionlessness.

時間を云えば、まだ然程長くはない筈だが。　長さに見合わぬ多くの機会があった。 Ayane Ichijouなる人間を知る為の。
In terms of time, it hasn't been that long yet.　But there have been many opportunities that do not match the length of time. To get to know Ayane Ichijou.

あれは、奇妙な娘だと思う。
That's a strange girl, I think.

つくりものめいていると、そう感じる。　人形のよう、という印象とはまた違う。
That's what I feel when I look at my creations.　It's different from the impression that it looks like a doll.

器械のようだと言い表すのが最も近い。
The closest I can come to describing it is that it is like an instrument.

人形じみた人間は、まず第一に虚ろである。　器の大きさに比してちっぽけな心しか感じられないから、ぽっかりと広い余剰空間が目に付くのだ。
Puppet-like people are first and foremost empty.　Because they can only feel a small heart compared to the size of their vessel, a large surplus space is noticeable.

だから人間の抜け殻――人形だと見られる。　　 Ichijouは違う。　余剰空間が無い。
That's why people see him as a shell of a person - a doll.　　 Ichijou is different.　There is no extra space.

正義の一念に固執するあの心は矮小にして狭小だ。　だが、それが相応に見えるのである。
That mind that clings to a single thought of justice is small and narrow.　But it appears to be appropriate.

少女の肉体は一つの意思、一つの理念、一つの目的を収める為だけのものなのだ。最初から。　それは人間ではない。　それは人形ではない。
The girl's body is only meant to house one will, one idea, one purpose. From the beginning.　It is not a human being.　It is not a doll.

それは器械だ。
It's an instrument.

（あいつは、不幸なのだろうか）
(Is he unhappy?)

かつて胸に去来しなかったわけではないが、明確に言語化するのは今が初めてだった。　その一問。器械は不幸であるか。
It's not that it hadn't occurred to me in the past, but this was the first time I had been able to articulate it clearly.　One question. Is the instrument unhappy?

人形は、きっと不幸であろう。　人の形に整えられながら人になれないのだから。
The doll will be unhappy.　They are made to look like people, but they cannot become people.

しかし器械はどうか。　器械として作られ器械として機能する器械。
But what about instruments?　Instruments that are made as instruments and function as instruments.

それは不幸であるのか。　　俺には答えを出せなかった。
Is that unhappy?　　I couldn't give you an answer.

わかる事は一つきりだ。　それが不幸であろうと幸福であろうと、器械は己に与えられた単一機能を果たし続ける。
There is only one thing to know.　Whether it is unhappiness or happiness, the instrument will continue to perform the single function it has been given.

壊れるまでずっと。
All the way until it breaks.

「あっ…… Minato-san」
It's ...... Minato-san.

足音を聞いて振り返った Ichijouが声を上げる。　呼んだのは実名の方だった。注意しておかねばならない――だが今はそんな気になれず、俺は黙って頷き返すに留めた。
Ichijou heard the sound of footsteps and turned around.　It was his real name that called me. I had to warn him - but I couldn't bring myself to do that right now, so I just nodded back silently.

どうせ誰も聞いてはいない。　花摘み娘の一団は自分達の会話に夢中だ。
No one is listening anyway.　The group of flower-picking girls are preoccupied with their own conversation.

「東側はもう一通り見たのか」
You've already looked all over the east side?

「いえ、まだ途中です」
No, I'm still working on it.

当たり前のように答える Ichijou。　……ここは城の西部である。 Ichijouに割り当てた調査区域とは全く反対だ。が、俺はこれもいちいち指摘はせずにおいた。
Ichijou answers as a matter of course. ...... This is the western part of the castle. This is quite the opposite of the survey area we assigned to Ichijou. But I didn't point this out to him either.

彼女を一人で行かせた時点で予測していた事だ。
That's what I predicted when I let her go alone.

「 Minato-sanの方はどうですか？」
How's Minato-san?

「それなりに収穫はあった。　詳しくは後で話そう」
I got a good deal out of it.　I'll tell you more later.

「はい」
"Yes.

快活な声だ。　しかし、間近で見ればさなきだに特異な少女の印象は更に明瞭だった。
She has a lively voice.　However, if you look at her up close, the impression of a very unique girl is even clearer.

 Ichijouを良く観察する者が一人でもこの城にいれば、忽ちに正体は全て露見するのではないか。　……そう思いかけたのは流石に偏執的であったろうけれども。視線を戻して、花畑の娘を見る。

The latter part of "Yorimasa" is a piece that mainly focuses on portraying the aspects of the battle as described by Yorimasa.　There is not much psychological description of the main character that makes the tragedy a tragedy.

能の舞台は舞台に非ず。　一つの世界である。
The stage of Noh is not a stage.　It is a world.

そう云う者がいる。　能楽師の力量が充分以上であるとき、それは完全に正しい。
